Japan Greatly Panicked by the Boycott of Japanese Goods in China

Decision to Submit International Prohibition Proposal

Dentsu, Tokyo, 10th: The Economic League held a standing committee meeting at the Industrial Club yesterday to discuss the proposals that the Japanese Committee should submit to the International Chamber of Commerce Congress to be held in Vienna, Austria on May 29th. As a result of the discussion, in light of the experience of China's boycott of Japanese goods, it was decided to submit an international resolution prohibiting boycotts of goods. The main points are as follows: Recently, boycotts of foreign goods have been based on political and diplomatic grounds in the Orient, causing the greatest obstacles to international trade. This not only has the worst impact on the nations involved but also disrupts peace between the countries and the world, which is intolerable. We hope that all countries in the world will eliminate the boycott of foreign goods as soon as possible. The International Chamber of Commerce, as the largest and most authoritative group of industrialists in the world, should take the lead in seeking the most effective methods to achieve this goal, which is an urgent matter. We hope that in the future, when concluding or revising treaties of commerce between two countries, clauses to suppress boycotts of goods should be included, and even further, the prohibition of boycotts of goods should be stipulated by international treaties.

The United States Does Not Want a Mussolini

Roosevelt's Authority to Reorganize the Executive Branch

National News, Washington, 9th After the US Congress passed the Government Economy Act last year, President Hoover proposed a plan to reorganize the executive branch, consolidate parallel branches, and eliminate redundant personnel. However, it was recently rejected by the Democratic-majority Congress. The US Senate passed another Government Economy Act, granting President-elect Roosevelt even greater authority to freely reorganize the executive branch. As long as it is within the scope of reducing government spending, the President can act expediently without seeking congressional approval. If Congress wants to veto it, it must have a two-thirds majority vote. It is now expected that the House of Representatives will also pass this new bill. However, the Republican side has already reacted strongly, claiming that granting President-elect Roosevelt unlimited power to reorganize the executive branch would be tantamount to creating a dictator, and the United States does not want a Mussolini.

Blizzard Disaster, 65 Dead

National News, Chicago, 9th Today marks the 63rd anniversary of the founding of the US Weather Bureau. Suddenly, a blizzard unseen since 1889 struck. The temperature in Chicago dropped to minus 19 degrees Fahrenheit, while temperatures in the northern states, western mountains, northeastern Great Lakes region, and the Canadian border area dropped to minus 50 degrees Fahrenheit. Although the center of the blizzard has now shifted eastward and its strength has weakened slightly, according to a survey by the Weather Bureau, no fewer than 65 people are known to have frozen to death, been crushed by cars, or been buried by collapsing houses due to the blizzard. The loss of livestock and other property is enormous. Detailed disaster information cannot be accurately known until several days later due to the disruption of telegraphs and the blockage of major roads in various places.

Moreover, in each ministry, there used to be so-called personnel departments only in the puppet State Council and the puppet Ministry of Finance. Now, all ministries and provincial offices have established personnel departments specifically for personnel

allocation and qualification assessment. They will not be employed unless the Japanese side believes that they will not oppose the puppet state. The personnel departments of each ministry are subordinate to the General Affairs Division or the General Affairs Department. The personnel departments of each provincial office are directly under the jurisdiction of the Director of the General Affairs Department. The heads of the General Affairs Division and the General Affairs Department are all Japanese. The organization of the department and the division is generally six sections. In addition to the Personnel Section, there are the Accounting Section and the General Affairs Section. The chiefs of the six sections are also all Japanese. Previously, the leaders of each province and department, in addition to their salaries, could receive some office expenses. Most leaders could manipulate the office expenses. Now, even a piece of paper or a pen must be obtained from the General Affairs Section of the General Affairs Department. If they spend a little more each month, they will be rebuked by the section chief. Therefore, the puppet ministers, department heads, and chiefs receive no benefits other than their salaries. The employment of personnel in each ministry is handled by the Director of the General Affairs Division, and the ministers of the ministry have no right to interfere. The situation in each province is better, but according to its system, if the governor wants to employ someone, he must submit a list, which is handed over to the Director of the General Affairs Department for review. The Director of the General Affairs Department then orders the head of the Personnel Section to investigate, and then submit it to the provincial government meeting. The Director of the General Affairs Department approves or rejects it. Often, a list of dozens of people results in only two or three being approved after their review. However, the issuance of orders must still be submitted to the puppet ministry by the Director of the General Affairs Department, and the personnel section of the responsible ministry must review it again. Chengdu and Chongqing Still Confront Each Other

Liu, Tian, and Deng Join Forces to Resist Liu Xiang

Liu, Yang, and Others Confer to Divide Territories

Chongqing Correspondence: Since the armistice of the Sichuan War, it could have ceased hostilities. However, in fact, there are still significant changes brewing, as Chengdu and Chongqing have become confrontational. Initially, Liu Wenhui and Liu Xiang, after signing a non-aggression treaty, concentrated their troops and telegraphed to return to the province. At that time, Deng Xihou, Tian Songyao, and Liu Wenhui could have had a conflict. Fortunately, elders in the provincial capital and generals of the Bao clique came forward to mediate and negotiate terms. The armies of Deng, Tian, and Liu then resumed cooperation. All provincial organs of Liu's army were returned by Tian Songyao. Tian, forced by circumstances, and because Tian's army had suffered great losses since the outbreak of the Sichuan War, while Liu Xiang had expanded his territory to more than 20 counties, and Yang Sen, Li Jiayu, and Luo Zezhou had also gained considerable benefits, deeply regretted his recklessness in being fooled by Liu Xiang. Therefore, he tried his best to express goodwill to Liu Wenhui and welcomed him back to the province. On the 24th of last month, Liu Wenhui returned to Chengdu. After Deng, Tian, and Liu met, they were not ashamed of going back and forth. Liu Wenhui was even willing to cede the position of Chairman of the Provincial Government to Tian Songyao. In addition to already telegraphing to the Central Government to resign, he also jointly guaranteed Tian's succession with Deng Xihou. Therefore, Liu, Tian, and Deng have gone from division to unity again.

On the Chongqing side, Liu Xiang believed that now that the war had ended, a meeting should be convened to discuss the future of Sichuan and the territories occupied by the allied forces. On the 3rd, a formal meeting was held in Chongqing. Those attending were Liu Xiang, commander of the 21st Army, division commanders Tang Shizun, Pan Wenhua, Fan Shaozeng, Wang Zuanxu, Yang Sen, commander of the 20th Army, Li Jiayu, commander of the New Sixth Division, and Luo Zezhou, commander of the 23rd Division, and more than 30 others. The first item on the agenda was the division of the territories occupied by the 24th Army. It was resolved that Nanchong and Wusheng counties would be assigned to Yang Sen, Suining, Fengxi, Zizhong, and Anyue counties would be assigned to Li Jiayu, and Tongnan and Lezhi would be assigned to Luo Zezhou. On the 4th, the meeting continued to discuss the establishment of the Sichuan Post-War Commission and the selection of candidates for Chairman, Vice-Chairman, and directors of each department. After pre-determination, Liu Xiang was the Chairman of the Post-War Commission, Yang Sen or Tian Songyao was the Vice-Chairman. As a result, Yang Sen politely declined, so Tian Songyao was decided, and Yang Sen was the Director of the Military Affairs Department, Deng Xihou was the Director of the Civil Affairs Department, Liu Wenhui was the Director of the Construction Department, Li Jiayu was the Director of the Finance Department, Liu Cunhou was the Director of the Industry Department, Wang Luji was the Director of the Education Department, and most people recommended Zhang Qun as the Dean of the Supervisory Yuan. The above are all general decisions, pending the formal establishment of the Post-War Commission before making a final decision. In the afternoon, the cases discussed were the suppression of the Reds. Liu Xiang advocated dividing the areas for suppression, with each responsible for suppressing the Red bandits within his own defense zone. Yang Sen advocated not dividing the boundaries, but unanimously uniting and suppressing to eliminate them as soon as possible. As a result, Yang's proposal was passed. On the 5th, Liu Xiang and Yang Sen both sent teams to Tongjiang, Nanjiang, Bazhong, Nanbu, and other places to assist Tian Songyao in suppressing the Red bandits. However, Tian is naturally suspicious. When the Central Army entered Sichuan to suppress the bandits, he deliberately obstructed it, vainly hoping to preserve his private defense zone. Now that Liu and Yang have sent troops into his defense zone to suppress bandits, it is feared that Tian will have another misunderstanding. (February 5)

Hunan Province Borrows Money to Build Roads

Constructing the Changhong Light Railway

Borrowing a Total of 50 Million from the United Kingdom

Changsha Correspondence: Hongjiang is the largest commercial port upstream of western Hunan. The annual export value of tung oil, wood, tallow, etc., produced there is tens of millions of dollars. Goods produced in Guizhou are also concentrated in Hongjiang and transshipped for export. However, land and water transportation are not very convenient, and the transportation of goods is extremely difficult. When Tan Yankai presided over Hunan's politics, he initiated the construction of the Changhong (Changsha to Hongjiang) motor road. More than ten years have passed, and it has not yet been completed. Last year, during the Double Ten Festival, Hunan welcomed Chinese and foreign experts to Hunan to visit and test gas vehicles. After the visit, Mr. An Lide, the American Commercial Counselor, made a vow to assist in the development of Hunan's construction industry and introduced the following two major enterprises: (1) Introduced Hunan Province to order 180 cars from Ford Motor Company in the United States, delivering 10 cars per month, completing delivery in one and a half years. One-third of the price will be paid when the cars arrive in Changsha, and the remaining amount will be repaid in installments within three years. (2) He introduced Mr. Freeman, General Manager of the British Investment Company in China, to Hunan to invest in the construction of the Changhong Light Railway. At that time, He Jian expressed his great welcome. In January of this year, Mr. Freeman arrived in Shanghai from England, and Mr. An Lide telegraphed He Jian to send someone to Shanghai to discuss everything. He Jian and Tan Changkai, Director of the Construction Department, and the members of the provincial government discussed the outline of the road construction, (1) The route of the light railway starts from Changsha, passes through Xiangtan, Xiangxiang, Baoqing, and Hongjiang, and then passes through Yuanling, Changde, and Yiyang to reach Changsha, forming a network. (2) The light railway must be connected to the Guangdong-Hankou Railway to realize intermodal transportation so that the products of Hunan and Guizhou provinces can be transported to Guangdong, Guangxi, and the provinces along the Yangtze River. (3) The light railway is a total of 2,000 li long, and each li requires 25,000 yuan, for a total of 50 million yuan in national currency. The full amount is borrowed from British merchants. (4) The loan is guaranteed by the Changhong Light Railway, and the principal and interest are repaid in installments from the road's income. The above method is to utilize foreign capital to develop the transportation industry. After the method was determined, Wang Huixian, an engineering expert and current Director of the Hunan Water Conservancy Survey Corps, was sent to Shanghai to represent the province. Introduced by An Lide,

Mr. Freeman was contacted. Mr. Freeman expressed his approval of the four measures set by Hunan Province, but attached two additional conditions: First, the 50 million yuan loan for the construction of the Changhong Light Railway must first be reported by the Hunan Provincial Government to the Central Government for approval and filing. Second, the chief engineer must be British, and all materials and vehicles should be purchased from British goods as soon as possible. Wang Huixian considered it feasible and returned to Hunan last week to report. Saving Sericulture: Please Restore the County Agricultural Station

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Industry, by order, dissolved the Wuxi County Agricultural Station, leading to the cessation of various agricultural and sericultural affairs. Subsequently, individuals from the sericulture industry, including Lu Zirong, Xue Shouxuan of the silk industry, and Qian Fenghao, stated that Wuxi's silk production had historically been the center of the province. However, due to recent pressure from Japanese silk and a lack of improvements, it had suffered a significant decline. They emphasized the necessity of providing relief and revitalization. Last year, the County Agricultural Station implemented a rescue effort, collaborating with the sericulture industry to establish forty guidance stations in the four rural districts, yielding considerable success and initiating advancements in sericulture. It was originally planned for this spring, drawing over nine thousand eight hundred yuan from the county's industrial funds, to cooperate with the sericulture industry to improve common silkworm rearing rooms in the rural districts and jointly operate sixty guidance centers, promoting the planting of one hundred thousand mulberry saplings, advocating for the replanting of old mulberry trees, establishing model mulberry gardens, and, to cultivate grassroots sericulture talent in various rural districts, recruiting female silkworm rearers and providing classes to teach sericulture skills. Since the closure of the Agricultural Station, sericulture has completely stagnated, with significant impacts on the social economy. With early spring already here and the silkworm season approaching rapidly, continued efforts are urgently needed. Therefore, they jointly submitted a request to be treated like the Zhenjiang example and to continue operations. The Provincial Department instructed the County Government to conduct a comprehensive review before approving the continuation. However, Lu and others believed that time was pressing and could not be delayed. Yesterday, they submitted a request approved by the County Government to the Provincial Department, seeking immediate restoration to facilitate improvements.

Luo Wengan Returns to Beijing Last Night

Inspected Two District Prisons Yesterday

Met with Judges of Various Courts and Gave Instructions

Luo Wengan, Minister of Foreign Affairs and Minister of Justice Administration, arrived in Shanghai the night before last with his wife and Zheng Tianxi, Deputy Minister of Justice Administration. Yesterday morning and afternoon, he inspected prisons in the Public Settlement and the newly established temporary drug rehabilitation center for criminals. Around 7 PM last night, he attended a banquet at the Italian Legation, and then took the late train back to Beijing at 11 PM. Detailed reports on various activities are as follows:

Prison Inspection

Minister Luo's visit to Shanghai was to meet with Acting Premier Song Ziwen to discuss important official matters and to send his daughters to Guangzhou. Yesterday morning, he telephoned Guo Yunquan, President of the First Special District Court of the Public Settlement, and met him at the Cangzhou Hotel. Then, at 9:45 AM, accompanied by President Guo, he went to inspect the prison on Xiamen Road for about twenty minutes. At 10:40 AM, he went to inspect the prison on Tilanqiao East and West Huade Roads, finishing at 11:30 AM. Luo expressed his satisfaction but noted several areas that should be improved.

Luo's Instructions

Accompanied by President Guo, Luo arrived at the First Special District Court on North Zhejiang Road at 11:50 AM. In the President's office, he summoned Shen Jia [blank], President of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, Yu Hua, Chief Judge of the Criminal Division, Li Dong, Chief Judge of the Civil Division, Guo Yunquan, President of the First Special District Court, Li [blank], Chief Judge of the Civil Division, and Qian Hongye, Chief Judge of the Criminal Division, and gave them instructions. He earnestly advised them on improving the judiciary and prisons, speaking for over fifty minutes, until 12:30 PM.

Reviewing Official Documents

After lunch, Luo went to the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on Fenglin Bridge at about 2 PM to review official documents and meet with reporters from various newspapers. At 4:15 PM, he went to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court on West Aximus Road to meet with President Liang Renjie and Ying Shi, President of the Second Branch of the Special District Court, inquiring in detail about the operations of the two courts, concluding at 4:40 PM.

Attention to Prison Administration

After speaking with the presidents of the two courts at the Third Branch of the High Court, Luo went to inspect the prison in the French Concession on Masnan Road at 4:50 PM. Liang and Ying, the presidents of the two courts, and Xie, the Warden of the detention center there, accompanied him during the inspection. Luo first inspected the administrative offices, then the conditions of confinement for Chinese and foreign inmates, as well as the attached factory, sick ward, and the sanitary facilities of the kitchen and bathrooms. At 5:10 PM, he went to inspect the newly established temporary drug rehabilitation center for criminals in the Second Special District at the Ladu Fang on Ladu Road, returning to his residence at 5:30 PM.

Expanding Prisons

During his inspection of the French Concession prison, Luo observed that the number of inmates was excessive, with up to four prisoners crowded into each cell, making it difficult for them to sit or lie down. He instructed Liang and Ying, the presidents of the two courts, to find ways to expand the facilities as soon as possible, and also instructed Liang to contact Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng.

Return to Beijing Last Night

Luo attended a banquet at the Xinghualou Restaurant yesterday afternoon hosted by the presidents of various courts, with Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng also invited to attend. Luo then took the night train back to Beijing at 11 PM last night.

Luo's Remarks

Yesterday, during his meeting with reporters from various newspapers, Minister Luo spoke about the past shortcomings in the judiciary and his views on future reforms. Luo first stated that there had been much criticism in the foreign press regarding the unsatisfactory state of the Special District Court, generally citing the following points: (1) excessive delays in execution; (2) excessive use of the right to appeal; (3) excessively complicated ordinary procedures; (4) insufficient understanding of commercial customs, etc. However, since taking office as the Minister of Justice, he felt that this situation was not unique to Shanghai, but was common throughout the country, where no one could honestly claim to be satisfied. Since the Maguan Treaty of 1902, Chinese law had been reformed to implement the rule of law, but it had completely adopted the continental system, placing too much emphasis on ideals without deeply considering whether it conformed to the actual situation. In Shanghai, where there are many continental expatriates, the majority are British and American. British and American law is simpler and more direct, so British and American expatriates are naturally even less satisfied. However, this type of law works well in Europe because its detailed provisions, such as investigation law, registration law, bankruptcy law, etc., are sufficient to remedy its defects. China's facilities are incomplete, yet it emulates others, which is like seeing someone dancing in a Yiyuan dance hall in the dead of winter, half-naked and ethereal, while we, without the same facilities, directly emulate them. Not only will we not be happy, but we may also become ill. Therefore, simply wearing a Western suit and thinking that one has learned the wonderful ways of others is not as suitable as wearing winter fur in winter and summer linen in summer. When he was in the Beijing government, he worked with Mr. Wang Chonghui to establish criminal laws and other legal systems, which at the time were mostly focused on scientific aspects, and he considered them satisfactory. However, after being in prison for a year, the experience gained during that year made him realize that the laws he had previously formulated were full of flaws and entirely unsatisfactory. From this, one knows that there is a great difference between ideals and experience, and that ancient Chinese law was not without its merits. As long as it is based on facts, it can achieve good results. For example, in the past, people emphasized the rule of man, and murderers often stepped forward to pay with their lives, maintaining a heroic spirit. Today, we emphasize the rule of law, but many people are cunning and disregard morality. He believes that cars can only be driven on asphalt roads; driving them on muddy ground will only lead to obstruction and make it impossible to drive. He also believes that governing with punishment is not as good as governing with righteousness.

Reforming the Legal System

Luo expressed that regarding the recent shortcomings in the legal system and the suffering of prisoners in prison, he had personally experienced these situations after being imprisoned for over a year. Therefore, he sent Deputy Minister Zheng Tianxi and others to various parts of China, including North and South China, to conduct investigations. After collecting their investigation reports and combining them with his own observations, he would compile a document and request the Legislative Yuan to reform the system.

Hope for Recovery

Luo expressed his great distress that the Shanghai Special District Court agreement had expired without achieving the goal of revision. At the same time, he acknowledged that there was a need to study the criticisms of delays in execution and other procedural matters. He hoped that active efforts would be made at this time so that the next time the agreement expired, it would not be extended and the goal of recovery could be achieved. Regarding the recovery of the right to manage prisons in the Public Settlement, Luo said that it would be difficult to achieve at this time.

Abolishing Special Laws

Finally, Luo answered reporters' questions, stating that regarding the issue of abolishing the "Emergency Measures for Punishing Crimes Against the Republic of China," some had proposed abolishing all special laws this spring. The laws concerning opium had already been abolished, but the remaining laws had not been passed by the Central Political Council. (New Voice Society)

Municipal Authorities Focus on Revitalizing Northern Shanghai

Only 30% Recovered After the War

Central News Agency reports: After the outbreak of the January 28th Incident, the houses in the Zhabei area of this city were almost completely destroyed by artillery fire. According to a survey by the municipal authorities, the losses were enormous. In terms of real estate alone, the area of destroyed buildings in Zhabei was over 670,000 square meters for multi-story buildings and over 250,000 square meters for single-story buildings, with an estimated total loss of over 29,963,000 yuan (losses from the destruction of the Commercial Press and the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Station are not included in the above figures). In Jiangwan, the area of destroyed buildings was over 76,000 square meters for multi-story buildings and over 44,000 square meters for single-story buildings, with an estimated total loss of over 3,640,000 yuan. In Wusong, the area of destroyed buildings was over 44,000 square meters for multi-story buildings and over 91,000 square meters for single-story buildings. In other areas such as Yinxiang, the destroyed area was over 13,000 square meters, in Zhenru, over 3,000 square meters, and in Pengpu, over 6,000 square meters. The losses in these three areas also amounted to over 310,000 yuan. In total, the area of destroyed buildings was over 1,210,000 square meters, with an estimated value of nearly 40,000,000 yuan. Over the years, the municipal authorities have been working to revitalize the area and cooperating with the people. However, the people's finances have been exhausted after the war, and the municipal authorities are also constrained by the limited financial resources of the city treasury. Although they have exhausted their wisdom, it has not been easy to plan comprehensively. Currently, it has been found that the area rebuilt by the people by the end of last December was only over 168,000 square meters, with a value of over 4,190,000 yuan, accounting for only one-tenth of the total, and nine-tenths of the area is still rubble. It is reported that the municipal financial authorities are actively planning to find ways to support the citizens' economy and increase their recovery power so that the area can return to its former glory as soon as possible and improve the city's appearance. Even if it is not possible to provide full assistance, it is hoped that half the effort can be provided. If the public has any opinions to contribute, they are willing to accept them sincerely for reference.

Social Affairs Bureau Announces Losses of Shanghai Factories in the War

Totaling 896 Factories

Totaling Over 53 Million Yuan

After the January 28th Incident last year, the direct and indirect losses suffered by factories throughout Shanghai have been repeatedly investigated by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and now the information is clear. The total number of factories affected is 896, with total losses amounting to 53,079,195.86 yuan. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau officially announced the detailed losses yesterday, as follows:

Significance of the Announcement

Shanghai is a city with a dense concentration of factories and the industrial center of the country. After the January 28th Incident last year, the Japanese invaders occupied Zhabei, Jiangwan, Wusong, and other districts and indiscriminately bombed them. The state of war lasted for four months, and the factories in the war zone were almost completely destroyed. Factories in other areas also suffered huge losses, totaling over 50,000,000 yuan. For the convenience of the world's reference, before publishing the statistics on factory losses in this city, we will briefly outline the preparation of these statistics as follows:

Source of Materials

After the outbreak of the war, the Social Affairs Bureau, in conjunction with the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Accountants Association, held a war loss registration, printed registration forms, and notified companies, businesses, factories, [blank] groups, and residents in the city to fill in the forms separately. These statistics are mostly based on these registration forms. However, the factory section of the registration form listed a total of 965 factories. After detailed sorting, it was found that some of them could not be considered factories according to the ordinary meaning of "factory". These materials had to be removed when compiling these statistics. After [blank] sorting, only 684 factories in this city filled out the registration form [blank] and reported losses. However, the war lasted for a long time, and all factories in the city suffered direct or indirect losses, while only one-third of the total number of factories in the city reported their losses to the registration office. In order to ensure accuracy, this bureau conducted a detailed follow-up investigation. However, due to limitations of time and resources, this follow-up investigation was limited to factories in the war zone. During the follow-up investigation, staff from this bureau went to the war zone to investigate existing factories. If they encountered factories that had not yet reported war losses, they would distribute registration forms and ask them to fill them in according to the format. Then, the existing factories were compared with the directory of factories obtained by this bureau in the previous year to accurately determine the total number of destroyed factories. Among all the destroyed factories, those that had not yet reported losses were investigated by finding the factory owner's address and inquiring about the exact amount of losses. However, in the case of 164 factories, their owners had moved around and could not be found after the factories were destroyed. The total losses of these 164 factories [blank] could only be estimated by referring to this bureau's old records and based on the factory's capital, product type, business conditions, etc.

Degree of Accuracy

The loss items listed on the war loss registration form are as follows: (Personnel Losses) Number of employees who died, were injured, went missing, were kidnapped, or became unemployed, and the resulting loss of monthly production capacity, as well as funeral expenses, medical expenses, and search expenses, etc.; (Property Losses) Houses, machinery, equipment, fittings, inventory, materials, etc.; (Indirect Losses) Bad debts, relocation costs, employees' private property, etc. There is also an average monthly operating loss item, which is calculated for three months for ease of calculation and included in the indirect losses item. Looking at the registration forms filled in by each factory, the personnel loss item was the most sketchy. Property losses were more fixed, and the reports filled in by each factory were more detailed. However, since most factories rented their factory buildings from others, the factory owners did not include the buildings when reporting losses. In the indirect losses, the bad debts item was estimated by each factory when the war had not yet stopped, so it was difficult to be accurate. Therefore, among the above three types of losses, the most accurate should be the property losses, followed by the indirect losses, and then the personnel losses. Many factories outside the war zone suffered indirect losses that were not reported, and it was impossible to verify them for a while. Also, larger factories with greater losses, such as the Commercial Press and the Yong'an Second Yarn Factory, all made detailed lists and reported them separately. Their reports only listed property losses.

Two National Goods Organizations Telegraph Request to Cancel the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement

The National Goods Maintenance Association and the Citizens' Association for Promoting National Goods telegraphed the National Government, Yuan, and Ministries yesterday, requesting the cancellation of the Sino-Japanese tariff reciprocity agreement: "To Chairman Lin of the National Government of the Capital, Acting Premier Song of the Executive Yuan, Foreign Minister Luo, Finance Minister Song, and Industry Minister Chen: We respectfully report that since the implementation of the tariff reciprocity agreement, our country's industry and commerce have suffered greatly. To list the most important points: (1) The goods imported by Japan into our country under Part A are numerous and comprehensive, totaling over 700 items, all of which are absolutely dumped on our national goods. On the other hand, the goods exported by our country to Japan under Part A are only three categories: silk, embroidery, and summer cloth. The disparity in quantity is too great to be equal and reciprocal; (2) Japanese goods shipped to China are subject to low taxes in our country, where tariff autonomy has not been fully achieved, and can be dumped as much as possible, destroying national goods. On the other hand, our three categories of goods shipped to Japan are subject to squeeze from high Japanese taxes, almost completely disappearing. For example, our silk used to be a major commodity sold to Japan and Korea, but Japan suddenly added a tax of 100% of the value. Although it has been reduced by 30 after several negotiations, it is still 70% of the value. After the tax reduction, no goods can still be sent. The tax reduction in name is equal to no reduction in fact. The Japanese customs officials arbitrarily estimate the cost of goods to be more than double, causing our silk and embroidery to be blocked by heavy taxes for nearly a year. Summer cloth is also being gradually eliminated, causing all industries to be depressed and on the verge of death. Under this serious situation, even without the tragic September 18th Incident last year and the occupation of the Northeast, this reciprocity agreement should also be abolished. It is difficult for the amount of tariffs to be equal and reciprocal. Therefore, the decline of national goods in recent years is entirely due to the dumping of Japanese goods with low taxes. If our government does not abolish the agreement in time, national goods will inevitably be defeated and have no foothold. Therefore, in order to provide a lifeline for the slightly budding national goods, it is necessary to abolish the agreement in order to save the crisis. The national economy and people's livelihood are based on this. Furthermore, since the Northeast was invaded and occupied by the violent Japanese and customs duties were forcibly seized, the taxes on national goods have been extremely high, increasing by 600 to 700% compared with the previous tax rates, and even [blank] times. As a result, the transportation of national goods to [blank] has been greatly affected and is likely to be impossible, following in the footsteps of Korea. The future of national goods is extremely painful. After a joint meeting of our associations, we respectfully request that the government, Yuan, and Ministries quickly announce the abolition of the agreement and implement tariff autonomy in order to protect the national foundation and ensure the people's livelihood. We are eager to await your order. The Chinese National Goods Maintenance Association and the Shanghai Citizens' Association for Promoting National Goods."

Huang Naishu Discusses Increasing Postage to Southeast Asia

Still Charging Half Price for Letters Sent Abroad

Small Increase, Little Impact on Overseas Chinese

Affected by the seizure of postal rights in the Northeast and the fall in silver prices in recent years, the Post Office has suffered significant deficits. Director Huang Naishu [blank] is aware of this difficulty and has spared no effort in seeking ways to increase revenue and reduce expenditures. Recently, he proposed to revise the postage rates between the Southeast Asian Islands and Fujian and Guangdong. Outsiders, unaware of the true situation, have made many erroneous reports. The Central News Agency reporter specially visited Director Huang to inquire about everything, which is recorded as follows:

Previous Situation

Director Huang said, "There are many Chinese living in the Southeast Asian Islands, and the exchange of letters and remittances is very busy. Therefore, there are private postal bureaus in Shantou, Xiamen, and other places to facilitate the overseas Chinese, and the postal fees collected are also very favorable. The method of posting is to pay according to the weight of the entire package. Since 1927, the postal bureaus in the American Philippines, the Dutch East Indies, and French Annam, etc., except for Malaysia and the Southeast Asian Islands, have requested reforms in accordance with the Universal Postal Union Convention and have implemented them one after another, abolishing the method of posting entire packages."

Preferential Treatment

"In 1929, British Singapore also made the same request. Our postal bureau could not oppose it due to the Universal Postal Union Convention. However, at that time, the overseas Chinese directly negotiated with the Singapore Post Office, and a decision was made on preferential treatment. At that time, the postage for each overseas letter from our country weighing 20 grams was 10 cents, with a 50% discount, only charging 5 cents. Letters sent from Singapore were charged 6 cents in Singapore currency, which has been implemented to this day without any change."

Three Price Increases

"In the past three years, the price of silver has plummeted, and our country's post office has suffered huge losses due to foreign exchange. Therefore, the price has been increased three times, from 10 cents to 15 cents to 20 cents, and to today's 25 cents. This year, due to the seizure of the post office in the Northeast, income has decreased and deficits have increased. If this continues, our country's post office will go bankrupt. Therefore, there is a proposal to revise the fee for Singapore postal items. After Postal Director Lin submitted a request, he went to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission to discuss it in order to proceed as soon as possible."

Still Charging Half Price

"Currently, the fee for each overseas letter is 15 cents, while the fee for letters to that area is still 5 cents, only one-third. At a time when the price of gold is soaring and the post office is facing difficulties, it is difficult to cope without making corrections. Therefore, it is proposed to increase it to 12.5 cents, which, although increased, is still half price. Moreover, overseas Chinese remit money, send letters, etc., at most once a month, or once every few months. The increased burden is limited. The income of overseas Chinese has also increased proportionally with the soaring price of gold. This small burden should have no impact. But for the post office, every little bit helps, and the annual income can be slightly compensated. I hope all circles will recognize the facts."

Silver and Banking Industries Express Support for Abolishing Taels and Replacing with Yuan

Regarding the abolition of taels and replacement with yuan, the Ministry of Finance has decided to implement new currency weights and fineness on March 1st. The legally defined exchange rates for silver dollars and silver taels have also been stipulated. According to interviews conducted yesterday by a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency with leaders in the silver and banking industries, if the nation wishes to unify its currency system, it must abolish taels and replace them with yuan. The new currency weights and fineness stipulated by the Ministry of Finance are based on the National Currency Ordinance of the Republic of China. Furthermore, during the initial implementation, the concurrent use of silver dollars and silver taels is permitted, and the stipulated legally defined exchange rates are not expected to cause any difficulties during implementation. Therefore, they are quite supportive. Moreover, after implementation, all transactions in various industries will be conducted using silver dollars, which will greatly simplify procedures.

Catholics See Off Archbishop Costantini Returning to His Country

Both Sides Will Inspect Today After Two Ships Collide

Families of the Deceased Resolve to Lodge Protests

The Taikoo Company's "Ningbo" steamer and the Zhongwei Company's "Taiping" steamer collided in the waters off Dongjiadu the day before yesterday, causing damage to civilian boats and drowning crew members and passengers. Yesterday, the two companies negotiated with each other and decided to conduct an inspection today. The families of the deceased will lodge protests. Details are as follows:

Negotiations Between the Two Parties

After receiving the report from the owner of the "Taiping" steamer, the Zhongwei Company immediately sent a letter to the Taikoo Company yesterday morning, stating roughly that their "Taiping" steamer was damaged by the Taikoo Company's "Ningbo" steamer at 11:40 AM on February 9th, causing damage to civilian boats and drowning fatalities. They requested that personnel be sent for inspection tomorrow morning. The "Taiping" steamer is moored at the Zhoupu Zhonghua Wharf. As for the damaged civilian boats and drowned fatalities, the Taikoo Company should be responsible for compensation, etc. After receiving the report from the owner of the "Ningbo" steamer, the Taikoo Company also sent a letter to the Zhongwei Company yesterday morning.

The letter roughly stated that at 11:40 AM on February 9, 1933, the Taikoo Company's "Ningbo" steamer collided with the Zhongwei Company's "Taiping" steamer at the Dongjiadu shipyard. The "Ningbo" steamer has now entered the Jiangnan Shipyard for repairs. Please send personnel to inspect it at 4:00 PM today, etc.

Inspection Today

Yesterday, when the Zhongwei Company received the letter from the Taikoo Company, they did not have time to send personnel for inspection. They immediately reported the situation to the Jianghai Customs Shipping Office, the Navigation Administration Bureau, and the Shipping Association, and decided that this morning, the two companies would jointly inspect the damage to the two ships with notaries and surveyors, and study the issue of responsibility for the collision. According to Zhongwei officials whom the Xin Sheng News Agency reporter met yesterday, the Ningbo steamer was believed to have been travelling the wrong route, and despite the Taiping steamer's horn signal, there was no response, leading to the disaster, and the Taikoo Company should bear full responsibility. Officials from the Taikoo Company stated that the Taiping steamer had already stopped and anchored, and the Taiping steamer should not have continued to advance, pushing the blame onto one another. Who is right and who is wrong remains to be determined after inspection.

Water Patrol Report

The Water Patrol Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau released a report yesterday regarding the collision between the "Taiping" and "Ningbo" steamers, stating that around 11:00 AM yesterday morning, they received a report of a ship collision at the Sanda Wharf in Puxi. Team Leader, Zhang Kefeng, and water police Wang Xuede, Lu Gengsheng, and Li Xiu were dispatched to investigate and provide rescue. The "Ningbo" steamer was outbound, and the "Taiping" steamer was inbound. As a result of the collision, the "Taiping" steamer veered towards the west bank, causing damage or destruction to the sand barges, sampans, and gravel boats moored alongside. In addition, a cargo ship that had just departed from the Guild Wharf was broken into two sections by the collision. All passengers and crew members fell into the water. One person, Shen Guanxi, was rescued with a waist injury and taken to Shanghai Hospital by the team.

Details of the Losses

The cargo ship, registration number 6688, which departed from the Guild Wharf and was heading towards the Wu Chong Jing area opposite Longhua Nandang Estuary, was captained by Wang Yugen. It had a carrying capacity of about 400 dan. Each passenger was charged only 15 copper coins for a round trip on the same day. On that day, it was carrying 29 passengers and 3 crew members. It was struck shortly after leaving the shore, and the ship was completely submerged in two sections. All passengers and crew members fell into the water. One person, Shen Guanxi, was rescued by the water patrol team and was injured. Another person, Zhang A Wang, was rescued by the Rescue Bureau but died immediately. The rest drifted with the waves. Fourteen sand barges and five sampans belonging to Yang Wanlin and other boatmen were damaged. One cargo ship sank. The "Taiping" and "Ningbo" steamers each sustained minor damage. The total amount of losses is estimated at around 60,000 to 70,000 yuan.

Issues Arise with Freight Costs After Rice Industry Adopts New Measuring Instruments

Rice Merchants and Laborers Hold to Their Respective Positions

The Shanghai rice industry has always used the Haihu (sea peck) as the standard for trading rice, with ten dou (pecks) making one shi (stone). However, the Haihu is no longer suitable for use. New measuring instruments have been adopted, with each shi being smaller than the old Haihu by one and a half dou, making it eight and a half dou. This has been implemented since the first of this month. All transactions in the market are conducted using the new measuring instruments. However, this has led to disputes in barge transportation, cartage, and porterage. Those who pay for the services believe that since the old system was based on the Haihu, and the new measuring instrument is smaller, the costs should be reduced proportionally. However, the barge operators and carters argue that they are paid per bag and cannot reduce costs simply because the quantity of goods is slightly less. Rice merchants now believe that the amount of rice sold daily in both the north and south markets exceeds 10,000 shi, all of which is purchased by rice merchants. Compared to the old instruments, this amounts to 1,500 shi less per 10,000 shi. Cartage and other fees are not a small amount. Monthly statistics are even more considerable. If the costs are not calculated and reduced based on the new measuring instruments, it would be unfair and a significant loss. Who can bear this? The carters do not understand the underlying reasons, leading to disputes. It is requested that rice merchants' leaders inform the cartage foremen and mediate the situation.

The Shanghai Minbao Newspaper launched Aviation to Save the Nation Gift Certificates. The detailed measures are recorded below: The call for "Aviation to Save the Nation" has been very loud. All Chinese citizens should do their part to pool their efforts and achieve the goal. However, the people have long suffered from economic hardship, and the difficulties after the war are even more pronounced. To enable everyone to contribute without being harsh or disruptive, and without harming oneself or others, a large amount of money can be raised in a single transaction. The launch of the "Aviation to Save the Nation Gift Certificates" by our colleagues is the easiest and most meaningful method to implement. Based on our humble understanding, we propose the following measures, hoping that patriotic compatriots will promote them together. This will fulfill the human obligation of "reciprocity" and the practical effect of "saving the nation and wiping out shame." We intend to first solicit 500 initiators in order to formally propose to the China Aviation Association for implementation. Anyone who agrees with this proposal is requested to immediately provide their name, address, and occupation to this newspaper so that everyone can easily collect, benefit, and achieve the best results. (2) Those who receive national salvation gift certificates will not issue power money or hold banquets, embodying the spirit of thrift while being patriotic. (3) When sending gift certificates, the sender and recipient, as well as the date, must be indicated on the certificate. It can only be used once and cannot be transferred. (4) Gift certificates are divided into wedding and funeral styles, with eight denominations: half a yuan, one yuan, two yuan, four yuan, six yuan, eight yuan, ten yuan, and fifty yuan. (5) The gift certificates are issued by the China Aviation Association and sold by various banks on commission. Each bank will establish an "Aviation to Save the Nation Gift Certificate Account." All funds from sales will be deposited into this account and reconciled monthly, with public reports. (6) Reputable and respected individuals and representatives of statutory organizations will be appointed to form a custody committee and be responsible for auditing. (7) All funds from this program will be used to purchase aircraft. Shanghai Minbao Newspaper, 201 Shandong Road.

Taxpayers' Association Negotiates Water Shutoff

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association wrote to the Public Works Department to negotiate the water shutoff issue with the Shanghai Waterworks Company. The letter stated: We are writing to you regarding the letter from the Huada Real Estate Company stating that since the Waterworks Company changed to using water meters, water bills have increased sharply, placing a heavy burden on the people. Our firm leases 100 houses in Yuanfu Lane, Tangshan Road. According to the previous system of bundled water charges, we paid 152 yuan and 20 jiao per month. Since the water meters were installed in July of last year, the price has been more than four times higher. Furthermore, the water bills for Shuncheng Lane, Kunming Road, and Shunzhi Lane in Zhoujiapai, Yangshupu, are also calculated according to water meters, making it impossible to pay. The Waterworks Company suddenly shut off the main water pipes in Yuanfu Lane, Shuncheng Lane, and Shunzhi Lane yesterday, implementing a water shutoff. We are writing to you to request that your association quickly negotiate with the Waterworks Company to immediately reopen the closed main water pipes to benefit the lives of the people. We believe that shutting off the water is not a fundamental solution to the water price issue. In the event of a major change that affects the lives of users, our association and your bureau will not be able to stand idly by. Based on the above situation, we hereby request that your bureau instruct the Waterworks Company to restore the water supply in order to protect the lives of the people and await a resolution. To the General Manager of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Shanghai International Settlement.

Chinese Sailing Vessel

Two American Youths Embark on a Brave Journey to Sail From Shanghai to New York

Accompanied by Adventurers Clark and Rufiu

Also Joining Are Two White Russians and a Chinese Captain

The "Great American Evening Post" reported that two American youths in Shanghai plan to set sail in a Chinese sailing vessel early next week, braving the ocean to fulfill their ambition of riding the long winds and breaking through thousands of miles of waves. The two youths are Belon Shied from Hutersdock, New York, and Vance Swords from New York City. It is said that this trip is only intended as a grand tour with no specific purpose or concrete plan, simply to set sail from Shanghai and hopefully reach New York. They are accompanied by adventurers Clark and Rufiu, two White Russians, and a Chinese captain. The ship is named "New Horizon," is only 65 feet long, and the main mast is 55 feet high. It relies entirely on wind power. The ship is also equipped with a small boat with a motor for towing the sailing vessel when entering ports. Their route is planned to first go to Hong Kong, then to Guam, and then to Honolulu. After passing Guam, they will tour the nearby islands to entertain themselves. After that, they plan to go directly to San Francisco, then take the Panama Canal to reach New York.

Zhang Baofu and His Wife Turn Against Each Other, Cutting off Water and Electricity Supply

Past Affection All Flows Away

Wife, as Agent for Their Son, Sues in Court

丨Judge Kindly Advocates Reconciliation丨

Zhang Baofu, the head of the accounting department of the Jianghai Customs, a native of Beiping, graduated from the Beiping Taxation School. In the 18th year of the Republic [1929], he married Ms. Xu, a fellow Beiping native and student at Xiehe School. Because both were Christians, the wedding was presided over by Pastor Huang. After the marriage, they came to Shanghai to work and lived together at No. 40 Yide Lane, Raul Road, in the French Concession. Their relationship was still harmonious, and they had a son named Pingping, who is now two years old. Recently, their love suddenly broke down, almost becoming enemies. At that time, Zhang ordered Ms. Xu to return to Beiping, but she refused. Zhang cut off the electricity and running water and did not give her any living expenses. Ms. Xu had no choice but to rent a pavilion at No. 50 in the same lane and live there. She also turned to the Women's Association for help. The association and several Christian colleagues from the Customs mediated several times, but all failed. Ms. Xu then sought a connection with a Western family to teach Chinese in order to maintain the livelihood of herself and her son. On one hand, she hired attorney Qiu Fenling to file a lawsuit in the First Special Court, with her son Pingping as the plaintiff and Zhang Xu as the legal representative, accusing Zhang Baofu of neglecting his duty to raise their child. She requested alimony for Pingping of 180 yuan per year until the age of 20, totaling 3,240 yuan in silver, plus 2,000 yuan for education expenses, and alimony for Ms. Xu of 500 yuan per year until the age of 60, totaling 32 years, for a total of 16,000 yuan in silver. In total, the sum was 21,240 yuan in silver. Because she could not afford the litigation fees, she requested litigation assistance. The Special Court approved her request. Yesterday morning, Luo Mou Tai, recommended by Wen Min's Fourth Tribunal, summoned Zhang Xu, the plaintiff, who brought Zhang Pingping to court on time. Zhang Baofu, the defendant, was unable to attend due to war affairs. His mother, Ms. Dong, represented him in court. First, the plaintiff, Zhang Xu, testified, "The defendant is now even more hostile to me than an enemy. Since August of last year, he has cut off my living expenses. I do not want to divorce the defendant. I only ask for living expenses to maintain my life. As for all the defendant's behavior, I do not want to announce it. It is not that I do not want to live with him, but it is because I cannot bear to live with him again." She said that the defendant's monthly income was more than 400 yuan, and he had promised to give her 150 yuan per month after she returned to Beiping, but her parents were not in Beiping, and she had no relatives, so she did not want to go there, and she only asked for 500 yuan per year, which was not too much. Then, Ms. Dong testified, denying that her son could earn more than 400 yuan a month, saying that his monthly salary was only 150 taels, which could be investigated, and hoping that her daughter-in-law could continue to live with him. The court held that in personnel lawsuits, the parties must be present in court, and that disputes between husband and wife were originally emotional. If a judgment was made by the official authorities, it would be difficult to restore affection. Therefore, reconciliation was the best option. The hearing was postponed and they were instructed to go outside and try to reconcile. If they could not reconcile, the defendant must be present in court at the next hearing. The judge would try to persuade both parties to make peace and avoid further litigation. After the instructions were given, the court adjourned.

Another Person Killed at the Flower Fair

Ma Zhitian Hangs Himself on Iron Bars

Ma Zhitian, a Muslim from Nanjing, 41 years old, who lived on the mezzanine floor of No. 34 Shenxiangge Road in the city, used to deal in chicken and duck business. He had a wife, Ms. Ma, and two children, a family of four, and their lives were very difficult. Ma did not seek to work hard in a proper way, but wanted to make a fortune through gambling. Therefore, he both played cards and indulged in flower fairs, which often led to a lack of food. Fortunately, his brother often helped him. The day before yesterday, because there was no rice to cook, his brother gave him five yuan. Unexpectedly, Ma used this as a desperate gamble, but he lost everything. Having no face to see his brother, he hanged himself on the iron bars of the window of the Wang Yi Ma Lane house behind his house. He was found dead by his neighbors, who notified his wife. The wife arrived and wanted to collect the body, but the Second District Police learned of it and ordered the local headman Jiang Pingyang to report to the local court for an inspection. Prosecutor Wu and others were commissioned to go to the scene, confirmed that he had died by hanging himself, and ordered the family to collect the body for burial.

They can be purchased as dancing costumes, decorations, and ladies' clothes, which are very suitable. The prices range from 6 yuan to 400 yuan per piece. The exhibition catalog and special issue of the association have now been printed and will be distributed to all sectors of society. The temporary office of the association will be moved to the Lake Society from today (the 11th) to handle all matters.

On Mutual Assistance between Entrepreneurs and the Financial Community

Wang Yansong Publishes His Views

Mr. Wang Yansong, Executive Committee Member of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and General Manager of the Silk Industry Bank, recently deeply felt the shortcomings of entrepreneurs and their impact on the financial community, and published this article for discussion by the business and financial communities.

At the beginning of the 21st year of the Republic [1932], China's industry and commerce encountered unprecedented difficulties. During this year, there was always a hidden crisis in the market. Now that the final settlement period has passed, all industries are generally stable. The financial industry has also achieved good results due to early preparations. This phenomenon was really beyond our expectations. However, the country is currently in distress, and the market is declining. Financial institutions should be cautious and careful for their own safety, and strive for prudence in lending. However, for the sake of developing industry and commerce, financial institutions should also take responsibility. There is more than one way to save the country and resist the enemy, and promoting domestic products is the only predetermined policy for our entire nation. Whether the promotion is effective and what the results of the progress are depend on the self-awareness of the people on the one hand, and on whether the domestic products can meet the needs of the people on the other hand. Although domestic product manufacturers have recently shown a tendency to progress, the fact that capital cannot be supplied sufficiently is undeniable. Because the capital is insufficient, the productivity will be limited, and there is no way to develop and improve. Therefore, domestic product production is nominally the responsibility of domestic product manufacturers, but in reality, financial institutions should also take responsibility. In this society of free enterprise and free competition, the rise and fall of national wealth depends on the prosperity and decline of business, and people in the world pay too much attention to the amount of capital and the level of interest rates, and ignore the character and ability of entrepreneurs. The richest country in the world is the United States, and the most developed industry and commerce is also the United States. In short, the ability of the United States to have what it has today is by no means accidental. Several years ago, a professor at an American university wrote a book called "The American Soul," in which he described the fundamental reasons for the development of industry and commerce in the United States, saying that Americans have a strong will and great energy in business management. One of the most insightful sections, which is sufficient for our reference, is "Mexico and South America are also emerging countries, with abundant products, fertile land, and mild climate. The breadth of their resources is comparable to that of the United States, and they have no less opportunities for economic activity than the United States. However, the reason why these countries have ultimately failed to achieve the same development as industry and commerce in the United States is not limited to one aspect, but the most important of these is the spirit of the people, because the perseverance, agility, and integrity of the South American countries are by no means comparable to those of the United States." We tasted these words, which are enough to awaken our deep reflection. Compared to Americans, how are the so-called entrepreneurs of our country today in terms of their spirit of doing things, willpower, personality, and ability? Most industrialists and merchants are concerned with immediate gains and are ignorant of long-term plans. They are extravagant in their personal enjoyment and only focus on the present in their business plans. It is nothing more than empty talk to talk about saving the country through industry in this way. Our country's various industries are in urgent need of development. The development of industry needs capital, but it also needs entrepreneurs with personality and ability. Credit is most important in the business world. If an industry is managed by an entrepreneur with personality and ability, then its credit will definitely be obvious. Once the credit is established, all parties will be happy to invest. As the Western proverb says, credit is capital, which is what it means. In recent years, there has been a lot of floating capital in our country's market, and the financial industry has a feeling of indigestion. Among financial institutions, they should choose entrepreneurs with personality and ability among caution, and give them full economic accommodation, so that domestic industries will develop day by day, and entrepreneurs should also fully cultivate and maintain their reputation, so as to obtain the convenience of financial accommodation. In this way, the financial community and entrepreneurs can be linked together, and the future of industry will be beneficial.

Japan's Foreign Trade in January

The Japanese Commercial Counselor's Office in Shanghai received an official telegram from Tokyo yesterday, reporting that Japan's foreign trade in January this year amounted to JPY 107,000,000 in exports and JPY 173,000,000 in imports, resulting in a trade deficit of JPY 66,000,000, an increase of nearly 50% compared to the same period last year. In addition, Japan's total trade volume with various countries last year was as follows:

Country Export Value (in JPY) Trade Surplus or Deficit

United States 445,000,000 Deficit 64,000,000

British India 192,000,000 Surplus 75,000,000

Nanyang 159,000,000 Surplus 63,000,000

Australia 36,000,000 Deficit 97,000,000

United Kingdom 59,000,000 Deficit 19,000,000

Regarding Japan's trade with China last year, the office received a telegram from Tokyo on January 18, stating that exports to mainland China amounted to JPY 147,000,000, with a surplus of JPY 69,000,000, and exports to the three northeastern provinces amounted to JPY 146,000,000, with a surplus of JPY 18,000,000. Furthermore, Japan's total export volume in foreign trade last year amounted to JPY 1,457,000,000, of which exports to the United States accounted for nearly one-third of the total. The total import volume was JPY 1,523,000,000, of which imports from the United States also accounted for slightly less than one-third, which is also worth noting.

Farmers Suffer from Spring Snow

Since the beginning of spring, it snowed the day before yesterday, and although the snow melted in the morning, the weather suddenly turned cold around 10:00 a.m. yesterday (the 10th), and the north wind rose again. Snowflakes flew in an instant, and soon turned into sleet, which did not stop until night. According to farmers, snow is beneficial to farmland, while spring snow is harmful to farmland. This year, there have been consecutive spring snows, and the harvest may be reduced.

Yu Yan Discusses Railway Business Reorganization (Continued)

丨Two Points Contributing to Future Policy丨

(7) Streamlining Rolling Stock Materials (A) The purchase and use of rolling stock materials are of great importance and constitute a significant portion of railway expenditure. Recently, our company submitted a report that was approved regarding the coal quantity for the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways. After chemical testing, it was determined that the No. 1 coal from Zhongxing and Kai Tou mines best met the needs of these railways. Previously, delivery in Shanghai cost $18.50 per ton, but now delivery in Pukou costs only $10 per ton. The railway's monthly coal consumption is approximately 15,000 tons, so this alone can save over one million yuan. (B) Consumption standards for rolling stock materials should be investigated and determined. There are significant differences in the amount of rolling stock materials consumed by different railways, with some varying by more than double. There must be instances of abuse and waste. Our company has already assigned experts to conduct practical research on material consumption standards, and a draft plan has been prepared. A comprehensive reform policy will be implemented soon. (8) Increasing Vehicle Utilization Efficiency The supervision of vehicle utilization efficiency has not been given close attention for decades, resulting in some railways having vehicles but not using them effectively, while others suffer from vehicle shortages. This has even led to various malpractices such as the private sale of freight cars. According to reliable statistics compiled by our company, out of every 100 freight cars, the actual number used on each railway is as follows: Qinghe 20.5, Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou 19.6, Beining 15.9, PingSui 6.2, LongHai 5.8, Jinpu 5.5, Pinghan 5.3, Xiang-E 4.7. Currently, across the country's railways, there are 12,000 freight cars, but the average utilization rate is less than 10 percent, which is deeply regrettable. The current remedial measures that have been communicated to all railways for implementation include: defining extended ton-kilometers, implementing nighttime loading and unloading, reducing loading and unloading time, reducing switching time, creating train timetables, etc., in order to increase efficiency. (9) Responsible Joint Transportation Conference This is of great importance. As mentioned earlier, a responsible joint transportation joint conference was held, involving the joint transportation office, the business department, and three other parties, to discuss and determine the national responsible joint transportation criteria. Another meeting is expected to complete the process. (10) Organizing Exhibitions of Products Along the Railway Lines For the sake of commercial and transport development, our office will hold traveling exhibitions in major cities, showcasing the products, output, transport volume, production site prices, sales site prices, freight rates, taxes, transport and sales locations, production seasons, and all related charts and statistics of each railway line. This will allow merchants in various cities to directly recognize the styles of goods, the quantities sold in various locations, and profit projections, directly promoting commercial transport and indirectly revitalizing domestic production, with significant benefits. The first exhibition is planned to be held in Shanghai, with over 5,000 items already collected and currently being counted, registered, and arranged for display. The opening is expected in mid-March. (11) Publishing Various Publications (A) Publishing a national travel guide to stimulate travel interest and serve as a guide for travelers. A thick volume is about to be completed. (B) Compiling a national product directory along the railway lines to enable merchants to better understand products from various regions. It has recently been sent to print. (C) Compiling a freight guide with detailed explanations of all freight-related information and procedures, allowing merchants to understand the actual situation and not rely solely on transport companies. It is currently being compiled. (D) Compiling a small booklet of railway information, to be distributed or sold cheaply to passengers and merchants, so that people can learn about travel and trade routes, and generally understand the real situation of the railways. It is also currently being written. (E) The Beijing-Guangdong Railway Survey Report is currently being compiled. (F) A comparative table of operating revenue and expenditure of each railway over the past ten years has been compiled and printed in a few copies for research purposes. (G) A report on military transport equipment for national defense has been compiled, including important equipment and transport capacity of each railway. However, due to the confidentiality, it is not appropriate to publish it. Mr. Yu also expressed two hopes: (1) Railway freight rates should be autonomous; (2) The railway's equalization and transportation policy should be realized, so that political power extends to the people, making things convenient for them.

Increase in Copper Coin Exchange Rate

Since the abolition of the silver dollar standard in this city, before the reopening of various businesses, small money changers and tobacco and paper shops were exchanging silver dollars for cash at a rate of 2,670 to 2,680 cash coins per silver dollar, 310 cash coins for five small silver coins (dimes), and 450 to 460 cash coins for a double dime (20 cent coin). Since the reopening of businesses, the exchange rate has steadily increased. Yesterday (the 10th), the exchange rate was 3,000 cash coins per dollar, and 490 cash coins for five dimes (20 cent coins), or twelve dimes (six double dimes). The exchange rate for dimes and double dimes was 490 cash coins. However, the posted exchange rate for silver dollars at the Jiangyuan exchange was already 3,020 cash coins, and 500 cash coins for dimes (double dimes). Within these two weeks, the difference in the exchange rate has been as much as 300 cash coins per silver dollar.

The company's Chairman Wang Yansong, Managing Director Chen Songyuan, Zhu Wenqi, Directors Sun Meitang, Ge Jechen, Zheng Zenan, Dong Hancha, General Manager Fang Jiaobo, Deputy General Managers Ye Jiaxing, Bao Jingdi, and all directors, supervisors, and staff warmly welcomed the guests. The guests expressed their full sympathy for the company's aim to promote Chinese merchant insurance and protect the interests of policyholders. It is reported that over 50 companies took out insurance on the same day, and the future development of the business can be assured. The company's opening declaration is transcribed below: The insurance business is of utmost importance, as it concerns the prosperity of society and the safety of individual lives. For decades, foreign merchants have controlled it, resulting in a monopoly. Compensation is often complicated. The Chinese people do not understand this, and when paying premiums and taking out insurance, they often do not carefully consider the options. They may be persuaded by introductions or attracted by low premiums, and then rashly accept the terms. When a claim arises, the company cites regulations, and the policyholder is unfamiliar with Western languages. Disputes arise and arguments ensue. As a result, payments are delayed, and discounts are arbitrarily applied. The businesses that suffer losses are unable to recover, and the lives that are affected lose their security. Is this not a regrettable situation? The colleagues of this company, in view of this situation, dare to use their desire to serve society to seek the welfare of the entire society and individual citizens, and to provide their knowledge for insurance-related consultations, to help policyholders choose companies, and to handle all post-accident procedures. They will strive, within the realm of possibility and within a reasonable period, to transfer the insurance business from foreign merchants to Chinese merchants, and to make the insurance process easier for policyholders. This is our humble goal. At the beginning of the opening, we hereby declare this.

Seek Medical Attention Immediately After Being Bitten by a Dog

A child surnamed Han from Hankou was bitten by a dog. Yesterday, he took a plane to Shanghai to seek medical attention at the Isolation Hospital of the Shanghai Municipal Council in the Public Concession. This matter has attracted the attention of many people. According to the opinion of the Health Department of the Municipal Council, it is still unclear whether the child is suffering from rabies. If it is indeed rabies, then seeking medical attention may have been too late, as it has been eighty days since he was bitten. The current Pasteur treatment is a preventive measure. If medical attention is sought immediately after being bitten and injections are administered, one can be safe after fourteen days. The incubation period for rabies is about forty days to half a year. If the injection is administered too late and the toxin invades the central nervous system, there is no cure. Therefore, anyone who has been bitten by a dog must seek medical attention from the Health Department on the same day.

Jiangsu Natives in Shanghai Initiate the Formation of a Provincial Association

Already Approved by the Party Headquarters for Record

The number of Jiangsu natives in Shanghai reaches over one million. Usually there is no unified group organization, so the spirit is dispersed, and all hometown businesses cannot be fully developed. It is more difficult to contribute to national construction work. Although each county has its own native-place organizations, they lack contact and are greatly hindered. Now, there are over a hundred Jiangsu natives in Shanghai, including He Yuanming, Tong Hangbai, Dai Yongchan, Hu Xingyao, Yu Yaoqiu, and Wu Xiu, who have realized this and have jointly initiated the organization of the Jiangsu Native-Place Association in Shanghai. They have already applied to the Municipal Party Headquarters for permission and have obtained Permit No. 101. The association is currently in the process of recruiting members and will be established soon.

Chinese Traveling to Taiwan Must First Get Vaccinated

The Osaka Shosen Kaisha (Osaka Merchant Shipping Co.) received a telegram from the Governor-General of Taiwan stating that smallpox outbreaks have recently occurred in Shanghai, Fuzhou, Shantou, and Hong Kong, and that they are infectious. Taiwan has implemented inspections. Overseas Chinese traveling from Shanghai, Fujian, Shantou, and Hong Kong have begun to be vaccinated this month. Chinese people going to Taiwan via Shanghai to Keelung and Kaohsiung must first get vaccinated at the Fumin Hospital in Shanghai and obtain a vaccination certificate. After fourteen days, they can purchase a boat ticket to Taiwan with this certificate. After boarding the boat, each person's certificate must be submitted to the ship's doctor. If they are deemed to be free of smallpox and epidemic diseases, they will be allowed to disembark; otherwise, they will be prohibited from landing and escorted back to Shanghai on the original boat. It will now be more difficult for Chinese to travel to Taiwan.
