Talks

Raking Up Old News

— Wu

A few years ago, because of a moment of "righteous indignation," I spoke up for the students and school authorities of Peking University, under the title "Peking Universities Get the Cold Shoulder." Unexpectedly, it caused Mr. "Xiao" to raise the issue of the southward transport of antiquities. Later, Mr. He Jiaqian of Ziyou Tan gave a summary, saying in essence: The southward transport of antiquities is for the sake of selling them for money. If university students could also be sold at a high price, then they would also be transported south in armored cars.

From this, it can be seen that the "backbone elements" of the country are far inferior to antique archives. The reason is clear. However, judging from the newspapers, it is inevitable to make us suspicious, because the authorities' good intentions are only to "decide to move south," and there is no mention of selling them. Moreover, they will be sent back to Peking in the future, but no date has been set. So our speculation is not as accurate as the resolution.

Whether archive antiques can be sold for money, I think everyone can understand. Since they can be sold for money, and they are also objects from the Forbidden City, their value is inestimable, of course, it is conceivable. If anyone can seize them for private ownership, of course, they can become rich to an unbounded extent, needless to say. Even if they are offered as tribute to the dynasty, the official position should not be lower than the first rank. Fortunately, there is a Shanghai that will last for all time in China, otherwise, what if they are looted by the "Huns"? Even if the area north of the Yellow River is all the land of barbarians, and the area of the Yangtze River basin with its spiritual mountains and rivers is designated as the capital of the Republic of China, our cultural and spiritual antique archives can still be transported by armored plane to the Pamir Plateau. When ten thousand miles of mountains and rivers all hear the cries of ghosts in the coming years, we will have so many treasures of the holy dynasty, so in our spirit, we will still not lose our status as a "land of culture and relics." As for whether we can fortunately send them back to the Forbidden City, let's wait and see. In case of unfortunate premature death, we can also write a note in our will, instructing our children and grandchildren to take a trip to the old capital.

Secondly, university students have no fixed price in the market. Mr. He is indeed saying the truth. What we hear about the trafficking of people is nothing more than children and women, and university students are not counted among them. However, we have also heard the story of Lincoln freeing the slaves, so it can be seen that after black people were conquered by white people, they were bought and sold by white people in the market. However, there may not be any university students among the black slaves, but at that time, will university students shed their original form as Chinese people? Because if this "long-term" continues, it is not completely without hope that China will be sold off piecemeal.

Science

Another Hair Dyeing Method

— White-Haired Youth

Previously, I saw the hair dyeing method introduced by Mr. Shen Erming in this magazine. The author is now thirty years old, and his hair is full of white hair, so he made it according to the method, but the result was not very satisfactory. Moreover, because it is toxic, I dare not try it more. Now the author has made a kind of hair dye himself, and the result is quite good. The manufacturing method is convenient, and there is no danger of toxicity. I dare not keep it a secret, so I introduce it below:

The hair dye is divided into two types, A and B, which are used in sequence. The manufacturing method is as follows:

Type A: Dissolve ten grams of silver nitrate in one hundred grams of distilled water to obtain it. However, ordinary water cannot be used, because ordinary water contains green compounds, which easily combine with silver nitrate to form a white precipitate, thus reducing its effect.

Type B: Dissolve 4.6 grams of sodium sulfide in one hundred grams of water to obtain it. Although this substance does not necessarily require distilled water like Type A, it should not come into contact with metal.

The above two types of liquid medicine must be stored in dark-colored (blue or brown-yellow) glass bottles, because white bottles, when directly exposed to sunlight, will change their quality.

When using, first wash your hair clean, and after drying it, use a small brush to dip Type A hair dye and brush it all over your white hair. Wait until it is dry (about five minutes) and then use another small brush to dip Type B hair dye and apply it. Because the two types of liquid medicine undergo a chemical change, forming black silver sulfide, which can adhere to the hair. To avoid affecting the skin of the face and neck, which may also be stained with black spots, you can apply a thin layer of petroleum jelly or other oils in advance. Wash with tooth powder and soap.

Liquid Hair Conditioner

Hair often becomes dry due to insufficient fat. Because the hair itself normally secretes an appropriate amount of oil, if the fat decreases due to pathological phenomena, it will inevitably become yellow, withered, and dry, and even fall out. Usually, washing hair is to clean it, but you also need to often apply oil-based products to replenish the lack of oil. Solid hair creams, such as Stanco, have already been disclosed in this magazine. Now I will introduce a liquid hair conditioner:

Raw materials: 35 grams of castor oil, 250 grams of almond (extracted) oil, 110 grams of glycerin, 13 grams of fragrance, appropriate amount of alcohol.

Manufacturing method: Place castor oil in a large cup and mix it with almond oil. At the same time, dissolve glycerin and fragrance in 500 grams of alcohol. Mix these two things together, stir evenly, and then add an appropriate amount of alcohol to make one kilogram of hair conditioner.

Non-greasy Hair Conditioner

To make hair shiny, people often use hair oils and creams such as Stanco, but oil can accumulate dirt, especially for those who often travel to and from the city, dust accumulates in the hair, which is not hygienic. Now I will list the manufacturing method of non-greasy hair conditioner:

Raw materials: 10 grams of tragacanth gum, 10 grams of glycerin, 20 grams of alcohol, 20 grams of rose oil, 240 grams of hot water.

Manufacturing method: First dissolve rose oil (or use other fragrances) and glycerin in alcohol, mix well, then place in a mortar, mix with gum, finally add hot water, stir constantly until cool, and you will get a smooth and clean hair conditioner.

The Illusion of a Dream

— Shen Bin

The sky was suddenly covered in a grey haze, the thermometer's mercury plummeted below thirty degrees, and dust, like smoke, rose from the northwest corner, gradually approaching, making a "whoosh! whoosh!" sound! Ah! The wind is coming! And it's carrying snowflakes!

I trembled in a small, low thatched hut. My wife seemed to be beside me, and we both shrank our necks, looking outside, white breath puffing from our mouths. The wind grew stronger and stronger, and the snow fell heavier and heavier. Instantly, the grey universe transformed into a silver-white world!

"Are you cold?" I asked my wife.

"How can I not be cold? But what can we do?"

We couldn't bear the bitter cold any longer. My wife gathered some wood scraps from the corner and placed them in a broken pot. I struck a match and lit the wood scraps. Suddenly, all the wood scraps blazed up, and my wife and I both laughed!

We sat facing each other, feeling a little warmer all over!

"Old Li!"

Suddenly, this voice came from afar, and we both watched where it came from.

"Ah! Xiao Er? How are you still alive? Didn't I see in the newspaper the other day that you were killed by the enemy at Yuguan?"

This was a surprising and unexpected thing. How could Xiao Er, who had been killed by Japanese soldiers a year ago, be here now? We only saw him wearing a tattered military uniform, and amidst the snowflakes covering him, we could faintly see patches of blood! He walked from afar, finally reaching our small thatched hut, and we invited him to sit by our brazier.

"Old Li! I didn't die! I didn't die?"

"Ah! You didn't die? Then why did the newspaper the other day report your death?" my wife said.

"I don't care about that. I didn't know anything about it. I won't die. I will live forever!"

"Good! Then I'll bless the nation that we still have our strong soldiers! Xiao Er, may you kill many more enemy heads!"

After I said that, we all laughed!

"Old Li! Let's not waste time with small talk. I have news for you."

"What…?"

"Shanhaiguan has fallen. There are more and more Japanese soldiers. They are now preparing for a general offensive against our Rehe. I'm here to tell you! Our government, which has been clinging to a policy of non-resistance, is now officially resisting. Tens of thousands of northern brothers and many munitions were transported from the central government to our Northeast yesterday. How happy we are! I didn't die, I won't die! Ah! Old Li! Isn't this a great time? Let's all go! The government is resisting. Let's all go and kill our enemies! We must recover lost territory and trample the three islands...

..."

He said excitedly, but my wife suddenly interrupted him!

"Really? Is the government no longer relying on the League of Nations?"

"What's the use of the League of Nations? It's just an organization for the powerful countries to divide the spoils. Now our government has finally realized that!"

"What?"

"Let's go! Hurry! Get weapons! Hurry!"

At that moment, we were walking in the heavy snow, running desperately. Suddenly, "Bang! Bang!" a few shots rang out! My wife suddenly fell to the ground in front of me!

"Ah! Ah!"

××××

I finally cried out loud, my eyes opened, and I was still sleeping alone in bed. The sun was shining on my window, and the Wang family across the street were setting off firecrackers with "bang! bang!..." Ah! Isn't today the Lunar New Year? Then I realized the illusion of the dream I had just had! I jumped out of bed in one go!

Chinese Smart, Foreigners Smart

— Yi Ping

Office workers who use the tram often hear the phrase "help a little" to freeload. Speaking of freeloading from foreigners, we might as well "help a little," benefiting others without hurting ourselves. Why not do this kind of smart thing?

But in the end, foreigners are smart, and this topic is discussed over tea and after meals. The reason is that the buses are equipped with many machines that only allow things to go in, not out. You buy a ticket with a lead coin. When you want to get off, you have to insert the lead coin into the machine. The ticket seller shouts, "No way out," and the passenger says, "Inconvenient." But you can't freeload with a copper coin. "Foreigners are really smart!"

The bus arrives at a stop, and the ticket seller, with a pitiful look, says to each departing passenger, "Help a little."

To get off, you have to insert the lead coin. Would the bus stop on a busy city street and have you jump out the window? But you don't know that the Chinese are also smart. They can pull the imported door, and while it's half open, a "helpful" friend, in a quick moment, sneaks out without paying.

"Help a little," the "helpful" friend says again to the second person freeloading from the foreigner.

To prevent the Chinese from freeloading, foreigners invented a machine that only allows things to go in, not out. Foreigners installed machines that only allow things to go in, not out, but the Chinese still freeload. Foreigners smart, Chinese smart?

Shop Clerk Communication

Brother and Sister

Editor:

I am a lonely, weak woman. When I was nine years old, Heaven took away my loving parents, leaving only my brother and me. Because there was no inheritance, I lived in my paternal uncle's house, while my brother went out to learn a trade. Now we have both grown up, and logically, my brother and I should be harmonious! But because we have different mothers, he treats me very coldly. In these few years, although we have exchanged letters, they have only been superficial pleasantries. Recently, it's been even worse. I've written to him several times, but he hasn't replied; I've visited him several times, but he avoids me; recently, it's said that he's been transferred to Nanjing for work, and he doesn't even bother to let me know his mailing address. The day before yesterday, I met his friend and learned that he has even declared that he doesn't recognize me as his sister! Judging by his recent attitude, this is certainly true. For the sake of a proper future, I want to formally sever my brother-sister relationship with him. I don't know if this is possible; whether I need to get his consent before publishing a declaration in the newspaper; or whether a one-sided declaration is valid.

I am currently working as a temporary clerk in my uncle's shop, and it seems that there is no future. I want to enter the film industry; I don't know if this is a suitable career for me.

I am really uncertain about the above two questions, so I am writing this letter specifically to ask you for advice, which I eagerly look forward to. I wish you

Good health, Wu Yu Ying

××××

Editor's note: The brother and sister of Ms. Wu, because of their shared hardships, should logically cherish each other and be especially harmonious. Unfortunately, her brother has the four words "different mothers" stuck in his chest, leading to discord and treating each other as strangers, which is indeed very painful. But we believe that Ms. Wu also has no reason to formally declare a severance of the brother-sister relationship. You should know that, legally, adult siblings have no restrictions on each other. Moreover, in fact, because there is no inheritance, there will be no disputes. Therefore, the continued existence of the brother-sister relationship will not cause any problems in the future, and can even be left as a chance for reconciliation in the future.

There are many careers suitable for women, and film is certainly one of them. However, this requires "talent" and "interest." Now many people are loudly shouting to overthrow "talent" in many things, which is certainly correct; but we still believe that in the arts, "talent" is indispensable. Imitating others will never be pleasing. As for interest, Ms. Wu should consider it deeply. You can't just look at the external glory of ordinary stars, but you must see the difficulties of their success. We dare not be dogmatic about Ms. Wu's talent and interest; in short, film is indeed a career suitable for women, as long as you have this talent and this interest.

Finally, we still have a question. Has Ms. Wu previously told her brother about her ambition to "enter the film industry"? If so, we also suspect that your brother's recent attitude may have something to do with this. But this is just his stubbornness, and Ms. Wu can ignore it. We hope that you will enter the film industry for the sake of art, we hope that you will succeed, and we hope that you will give your stubborn brother no excuse, and that he will be speechless.

Letter

I have repeatedly seen in your newspaper that several readers want Mr. Lüshuang to answer questions about artificial ivory, but Mr. Lüshuang has not yet replied. I dare not boast myself, but recently I read in an old book about three methods of making artificial ivory, so I have recorded them for readers who want to try them. Furthermore, for those methods that fail or are ineffective, the responsibility lies with the author or the person doing the experiment. Shi Zhirang

Artificial Ivory (1) Seven taels of fine eggshell powder, three taels of fine plaster powder, and white and pure fish glue dissolved in water as appropriate. First, mix the eggshell powder and plaster powder thoroughly, pour in the glue water, and grind. Coat the inside of the wooden mold (which can be any shape) with lard, and put the previously prepared material into the mold. Let it stand for seven days and take it out to dry in the shade. It will be no different from real ivory.

(2) Pour ten taels of clear water and mix with eight qian of sulfuric acid to make dilute sulfuric acid. Then, put in five taels of peeled potatoes (i.e., Chinese yam beans, which taste like moss and are small in shape, often used in Western dishes) and soak for sixty hours. Then, filter through a bucket and squeeze dry the remaining material. Use strong force to make a solid body, and wait until it is completely dry to become the hardest ivory, which can be carved into objects at will.

(3) One tael each of fish glue, brandy, and fine eggshell powder, mix together, and add a little heat to make a mud-like substance. Stir thoroughly and put it into the mold. After it cools, it becomes solid ivory.

Novel

A Scholarly Family (17 Continued)

— Wang Zhongxian

Ah Li kept calling Ruo Hua "Madam," which annoyed Ruo Hua. In front of Ah Li, she beat Mao Sheng again, which was clearly "striking his body, shaming my face." How could Ah Li put up with it? She relied on the fact that Madam had recognized her as a daughter and, with the status of a young lady, was able to compete with the concubine. She argued with Ruo Hua, and neither would give in. In the end, Dai Qiu came out and persuaded Ah Li to leave.

Ruo Hua thought that Ah Li was a sent-off maidservant and shouldn't be so presumptuous, so she ordered Lao Hu to notify Sang Aqiang and give him one month to return the house, and forbid him from opening a tailor shop in the room between the walls. Who knew that Sang Aqiang's attitude was very tough? He took out a lease, saying that the Xia family had signed a twenty-year lease agreement with him. If the landlord wanted to take back the house, he would have to compensate him for twenty years of business losses, limited to at least three hundred yuan per month. This amount of loss would not be enough to compensate him even if the landlord's property was sold.

Ruo Hua listened to Lao Hu's reply and discussed it with Youzhong, but they couldn't do anything about Sang Aqiang. They could only scold the deceased Madam and admonish Mao Sheng not to cause trouble at the tailor shop in the future.

(9) Brothers are like limbs, wives are like clothes

Xia Zhongnan fell, and lawsuits accusing him came flying like snowflakes. Most of the lawsuits said that his concubine Ai Ruo Hua had taken bribes and sold positions. This was all that Madam had done behind the Master's back, and the person who handled it was Fifth Master Xia Youzhong. After the case was exposed, Zhongnan was still confused. No wonder Youzhong fled overnight with his sister-in-law as soon as he heard the news of Zhongnan's detention. It turned out that they were the main culprits in bribery and corruption.

Money that goes into the pockets of officials is like Jiang Ziya selling ashes—a gust of wind blows it all away. To get the original thing back is like "dried fish hanging on the tip of your nose"—don't even think about it! Xia Zhongnan was imprisoned for more than a year. He could only risk his old life, but he couldn't squeeze any money out of him. Everyone knew that his ill-gotten gains had long been taken back by his brother and wife, but his hometown was located in a place that the political power of the Tiannan government could not reach, so there was no way to confiscate his family property to compensate. What good would it do to force him to death?

Zhongnan was kept in a damp and filthy detention room for a year and a half and gradually developed hemiplegia. He was transferred to a hospital, where he stayed for a few months. The superiors saw that they really couldn't squeeze any oil out of the stone and that someone had come to intercede for him, so they were happy to do a favor and released him.

After regaining his freedom, he immediately telegraphed home to tell his wife to come to the dock to meet him. He set off northward by boat that night. When the boat arrived at his hometown, Ruo Hua brought her daughter and brother Youzhong to welcome him. They saw that his face was swollen, his hair was white, his appearance was very haggard, and he couldn't move half of his body. He had become a fresh, living dead man. Youzhong brought a strong servant named Ah Hai, who carried the Second Master ashore, put him in a car, and then brought him back.

After Zhongnan returned home, his two old brothers, Bodong and Jibei, came to visit him once. Youzhong accompanied him every day, chatting and laughing. However, Ruo Hua treated him very coldly. On the other hand, Dai Qiu served him very diligently. Ruo Hua always said bad things about her son Mao Sheng in front of him, because she said such bad things about the child, it aroused Zhongnan's suspicion. He thought that although Mao Sheng was not promising, he was not necessarily so bad, and that she must be treating her son with the heart of a stepmother. Therefore, he began to look at Mao Sheng in a different light. Because he was protecting the child's petty details, the old couple often had arguments.

Ruo Hua often dressed up in gorgeous clothes and went out to play and socialize. Zhongnan lay in his chair and watched, feeling really angry. He had advised her many times, but she just wouldn't listen. One day, she changed into bright clothes and walked past him with coquettish gestures. He called out to her and asked softly: (To be continued)
